<userid>101561798495470327105< /userid>< Review>
Love Redlands Market Night, also known as Redlands Farmers Market. This market night has been around and consistently held since 1988! It is considered one of the most successful Market Nights in Southern California.

It's held every Thursday night 6pm to 9pm. Redlands Market Night never happens on any Thursday after Christmas or New Year‚Äôs Day.

Be careful parking on State Street on any Thursday afternoon: the city is hyper-sensitive about cars parked on the street after their cut-off time leading up to Market Night. We have literally witnessed tow trucks lining up and towing multiple cars! Every week!

By the way, my favorite real estate company, Garrigus Real Estate, is located on State Street too! üòé< /Review>

< UserId.>
106905225698760043032</UserId.>
<Rate>5< /Rate>< Response>
None<//Response>
<text>BIG night market with lots to see. There's a farmer's market section, but most of the market is just different booths selling things - both food and non food. There's always some booth giving out things or with a spinning wheel. There's also a food pantry booth so you can bring canned goods to donate. Fun for kids, couples, friends - whoever.

I should add that there's actually a lot of food that you could have for dinner. Yes, there's the typical junk food like churros and funnel cake, but there's also substantial dinner food - tamales, Indian curries, etc. There's plenty to try, so you could come week after week and keep getting new things. Most places offer samples, too.

And parking isn't that bad if you come right at the beginning.<//text>< time>
1557338439637< /time>

< Review>
A collection of tisanes and teas that can be enjoyed by anyone. This is not a specialty tea shop. Their base green tea, a Gyokuro, is sold in fine grass-like clippings rather than whole leaf. Its seaweed flavor, to be expected, is rather violently enriched by a thick creamy mouth feel. I did not enjoy it. The Pue-Rh is sold loose, not in packed disks or in any many that would allow for it to continue to age. It's flavor was of rich tobacco, but unfortunately it's tobacco flavor was harsh and spicy. In addition one must carefully pick the full leaves out from amongst many crushed bits in order to avoid unnecessary astringency. But, if you're looking for flavored teas and tisanes this would be a good place to go. I had a 'Forever Nuts' tea made in house and I enjoyed it enough. For high quality tea this is not the place. Nor does it try to be. I recommend getting their signature blended tisanes.</Review>

< Review>
Of the many vets I have worked with, Dr. Hazanow ranks at the very top. She helped us care for Aidan, our Irish Setter dog, in his elder years. He enjoyed a long life for his breed, but the last couple of years was tough, as he developed bladder disease and complications. Dr. Hazanow provided empathic problem-solving care that was clinically competent and highly attuned to both Aidan's needs and our needs as his caregivers. Never were we rushed through an appointment. Charges are reasonable and I never felt that anything being recommended--procedures, medications, or other care products--had any taint of profit motive. Indeed, Dr. Hazanow several times suggested cost-effective solutions available from the drugstore or the supermarket. When she was not available, Drs. Knobel and Whitaker could also be relied on to provide excellent patient and family centered care, and the support staff were competent and very helpful. A couple minor front desk problems I experienced could have happened anywhere and the staff were apologetic and quick to fix them. Seven Hills is a veterinary practice and facility where you and your family can expect high quality, respectful client-centered services and supports for your pet.</Review>

<Date>1537472832380< /Date>< rating>

< review>
Warning: some mildly graphic medical details in the post.

I first found West Coast a little over three years ago when I first moved to San Diego.  I knew we were looking to add to our family soon and wanted an office that catered to OB and Gyn needs. I found them pleasant, easy to work with, not pushy with pill based contraceptives like some places I've visited (they give me rare stroke-like migraines so I cannot take them). You do pay for co-pays and such up front so be prepared.

Once pregnant a year later, I was assigned Dr. French whom I met a few times.  Patients do see multiple doctors during the pregnancy, so if you don't like this option, you should go elsewhere.  I was fine with this and appreciated getting to know different doctors.  I had a bit of bleeding early on and they were able to see me right away and confirm that everything was alright, though I had low Iron levels.  I opted for a c-section but was a good candidate for a VBAC having had an emergency one with my first child, but they thoroughly explained all my options and let me really make the decision.

Day of birth I was at Sharp Mary Birch, everyone was really nice and attentive and it went so smoothly in less than 45 minutes!  During recovery on the second day, I had some incision line bleeding and Dr. French recommended a blood transfusion and iron infusion.  Again, she explained the risk/benefit and let me make the choice since it wasn't a medical necessity.  After the procedure, I felt so much better and was glad I made the right choice!!!!

Follow up care at 6 weeks after birth was fast and they really were nice and made sure I was handling the new baby and myself well.  18 months later I am healed well and have a very flat low-line scar. If my insurance through work hadn't changed I would still be with them!

I highly recommend morning appointments and once you start going bi-weekly and weekly to schedule your appointments as far in advance as you can.  It'll make your life easier!  One downside is that their parking lot is kind of the pits, but there is parking across the street at the Sharp-Reese Steely building that is easier to navigate and find a spot.</review>

< Text>
This review is for the North County office - during my VERY complicated pregnancy, I saw Dr. Meshkat, Dr. Goodwin, Dr. Saffer, and Dr. Chirico. From my second trimester on, I had to be monitored heavily due to my son having a 1:31 chance of Down Syndrome and Intrauterine Growth Restriction. The last two months of my pregnancy, I was monitored several times a week, and each time, the doctors had a plan and always assured me that my son would be okay, even if he had to be delivered early.

He ended up being delivered via C-section by Dr. Hoover, and she did an amazing job. My son was born at 34.5 weeks at just 3 pounds because he was no longer growing in the womb, and his survival is totally attributed to the careful and difficult decisions made by these amazing doctors.

My son had a 3 week stay in the NICU at Sharp Mary Birch and I received several visits from these doctors just to see how we were doing, which meant so much during such a difficult season.

I'm happy to report my son does not have any genetic issues and is a perfectly healthy 4 month old :)

Maria (the nurse) and Beverly (the receptionist) are also wonderful - because of my frequent appointments, they became friends and support for my husband and I!

If we choose to have another baby, it will certainly be under the care of this incredible group of people.< /Text>

< Review>
BEWARE of West Coast OBGYN and Dr. Goodwin!!!  My wife and I are first time expectant parents and picked West Coast Obgyn and Dr. Goodwin because we thought that since they were next door to Sharp Medical Center (top rated in SoCal) they would be a good office.  NO SO!!!  First of all, one would expect when paying to see a licensed doctor / obgyn, you would see one, however, West Coast Obgyn makes it a business practice to use nurse practitioners and assistant nurses 90% of the time to consult and answer your questions.  My wife had had a miscarriage months back so we were very anxious to find out if our current pregnancy was healthy.  After sending us off to multiple expensive blood tests and ultrasounds (we are paying out of pocket, mind you), all we get is to speak with are the doctor's assistant nurses (not even nurse practitioners)--and I should mention that we had to hound their offices with calls three times a day before someone would call us back with results!!!

After over three weeks of mixed diagnosis, my wife FINALLY was able to speak with Dr. Goodwin who gave her a COMPLETELY different diagnosis than the previous nurses just days before.  And when my wife asked her why the diagnosis was so different and if there is something wrong with her pregnancy, Dr. Goodwin rudely snapped back 'how would she know, she wasn't the one who spoke with my wife last time'... My wife felt that Dr. Goodwin had absolutely no compassion towards her.  Her tone was irritated and that she just wanted to get off the phone.

After spending over a $1,000 in less than 3 weeks out of pocket, my wife and I are DONE with West Coast OBGYN. They obviously place making money by churning more patients through their doors WELL over caring for their patients as care givers.  My wife and I almost NEVER write reviews, but if this one will spare other people the pain we went through with West Coast OBGYN and Dr. Goodwin, then it was well worth the time.  We strongly feel we would have received better care and more compassion from a free clinic.</Review>

< Review>
I have to say (which I normally don't), THIS PLACE IS WORTH IT!  Although the service was slow, (i think they lost a cook because of the 'cook needed' sign), the food is great.  I tried various taco types, Carne asada, chicharron, adobada, cabeza and chorizo.  All were really good.  The tortillas were fresh and soft and the salsas are VERY GOOD. Gabriel Iglesias, thank you for the recommendation.  Loved the tacos.</Review>
